**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

Breaking political news

Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

# DAILY BRIEFING: APRIL 2025

## 1. Executive Power and Constitutional Challenges

### 1.1 Institutional Resistance (Harvard)
Harvard University has taken a firm stand against the Trump administration, refusing to comply with demands for changes [1] despite risking approximately $9 billion in federal funding [2]. The university has rejected subsequent compromise deals [3], establishing a significant institutional challenge to executive authority.

[1] Harvard Says It Will Not Comply With Trump Administration’s Demands, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/04/14/us/harvard-trump-reject-demands.html;  
[2] Harvard defies Trump’s demands and risks $9 billion in federal funding, https://apnews.com/article/harvard-trump-administration-federal-cuts-antisemitism-0a1fb70a2c1055bda7c4c5a5c476e18d;

─────────────────────────────────────────────

### 1.2 Legal and Judicial Responses
Multiple reports characterize the current situation as a "Constitutional Crisis" [1]. Tensions between the executive branch and judiciary have escalated, with the administration reportedly "mocking the Supreme Court" [2]. El Salvador's President Bukele has refused to release a wrongly deported Maryland resident, with critics suggesting "there is no law but Trump's law" [3].

[1] The Constitutional Crisis Is Here, https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2025/04/bukele-trump-court-order/682432/;  
[2] Why Trump and His Admin Are Publicly Mocking the Supreme Court, https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/politics-features/trump-mocking-supreme-court-1235317269/;

─────────────────────────────────────────────

### 1.3 Executive Orders and Authority Expansion
Recent executive orders have raised concerns about expanding presidential authority. One analysis characterizes Trump's latest executive order as revealing "authoritarian ambitions" [1]. In a concrete example of these orders' effects, the Gannett media company has stopped publishing diversity information in response to a Trump executive order and has removed mentions of "diversity" from its corporate site [2].

[1] Trump’s Latest Executive Order Lays Bare His Authoritarian Ambitions, https://newrepublic.com/article/193854/trump-justice-dept-executive-order-taylor-krebs-authoritarian;

## 2. Immigration and Deportation

### 2.1 Deportation Policies and Rhetoric
The Trump administration has significantly escalated deportation rhetoric, with the President explicitly suggesting that some U.S. citizens could be deported to El Salvador [1]. Trump has praised El Salvador's prison system and suggested it should be expanded to accommodate "home-grown" Americans [2]. The administration emphasizes alleged gang connections when discussing immigrants, though officials sometimes fail to substantiate these claims in court [3]. Christian immigrants who supported Trump's election now find themselves at risk of deportation [4].

[1] Trump calls for deporting some citizens to El Salvador, testing US law, https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/trump-wants-deport-some-us-citizens-el-salvador-2025-04-14/;  
[2] Trump says ‘home-grown’ Americans are next to go to El Salvador, tells Bukele ‘gotta build about five more places’, https://nypost.com/2025/04/14/us-news/trump-says-home-grown-americans-are-next-to-go-to-el-salvador-tells-bukele-gotta-build-about-five-more-places/;  
[3] Trump officials push immigrant gang message, but sometimes don't back it up in court, https://www.reuters.com/world/us/trump-officials-push-immigrant-gang-message-sometimes-dont-back-it-up-court-2025-04-13/;

─────────────────────────────────────────────

### 2.2 The Abrego García Case and Legal Challenges
The case of Kilmar Abrego García, a Maryland resident wrongly deported to El Salvador, has become a focal point of immigration disputes. El Salvador's President has stated he won't return García [1], while the Washington Post's editorial board has called for his return [2]. The administration's claim that it cannot return García is reportedly false [3], and there are calls for DHS and State Department officials to provide testimony [4]. Meanwhile, a judge has ordered the administration not to remove Venezuelans after the ACLU argued they were being "persecuted" as criminals [5].

[1] Salvadoran President Says He Won’t Return Wrongly Deported Man, https://www.nytimes.com/video/world/americas/100000010110367/bukele-trump-deported-man.html;

[3] The Trump administration says it can’t return Kilmar Abrego Garcia. That’s false., https://www.msnbc.com/opinion/msnbc-opinion/trump-administration-says-cant-return-kilmar-abrego-garcia-s-false-rcna201198?cid=sm_npd_ms_wa_ma;

### 2.3 ICE Operations and Enforcement
Immigration and Customs Enforcement operations have expanded in scope and location. The U.S. Army is now controlling land along the Mexico border where migrants could be detained [1]. ICE has detained Mohsen Mahdawi, a Palestinian green card holder and Columbia University student, during his citizenship interview [2], and additional Columbia students allegedly for pro-Palestinian activism [3]. In another case, the Department of Homeland Security incorrectly told a U.S. citizen who works as an immigration attorney to leave the country [4].

## 3. Foreign Policy and International Relations

### 3.1 Russia-Ukraine Conflict
Following a missile strike on Sumy that killed 35 people, Trump characterized it as a "mistake" [1], while European foreign ministers suggested "Putin is mocking Trump" and called for new sanctions [2]. Russia has reportedly targeted Sumy again [3]. Ukrainian President Zelensky has urged Trump to visit Ukraine before finalizing any deal with Russia [4]. The conflict has energy security implications for Europe, with EU nations facing a "dilemma" about potentially returning to Russian gas imports under Trump's foreign policy [5].

Signs of strain in international relations are evident. ## 4. Economic and Trade Policy

### 4.1 Tariffs Implementation and Challenges
The Trump administration's tariff policies face significant legal challenges, with lawsuits filed in the U.S. Court of International Trade [1]. Business groups argue that trade deficits do not constitute an emergency justifying these measures [2]. Reports indicate Trump is considering pausing auto tariffs amid global economic turbulence described as "whiplash" [3]. The administration's broader trade strategy is characterized as a "mess" by diplomatic sources [4].

### 4.3 Federal Budget and Spending Cuts
The Trump administration has proposed substantial spending cuts across multiple areas. A $9 billion spending reduction would target NPR, PBS, and foreign aid [1], while a separate plan would slash State Department funding by nearly half and reportedly end all funding for NATO and the UN [2]. Critics argue that these cuts, combined with tariff policies, appear designed to "move America down the value chain" by reducing scientific research funding [3].

### 2.1 Deportation Policies and Rhetoric
The Trump administration has significantly escalated deportation rhetoric, with the President explicitly suggesting that some U.S. citizens could be deported to El Salvador [1]. Trump has praised El Salvador's prison system and suggested it should be expanded to accommodate "home-grown" Americans [2]. The administration emphasizes alleged gang connections when discussing immigrants, though officials sometimes fail to substantiate these claims in court [3]. Christian immigrants who supported Trump's election now find themselves at risk of deportation [4].

[1] Trump calls for deporting some citizens to El Salvador, testing US law, https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/trump-wants-deport-some-us-citizens-el-salvador-2025-04-14/  
[2] Trump says 'home-grown' Americans are next to go to El Salvador, tells Bukele 'gotta build about five more places', https://nypost.com/2025/04/14/us-news/trump-says-home-grown-americans-are-next-to-go-to-el-salvador-tells-bukele-gotta-build-about-five-more-places/  
[3] Trump officials push immigrant gang message, but sometimes don't back it up in court, https://www.reuters.com/world/us/trump-officials-push-immigrant-gang-message-sometimes-dont-back-it-up-court-2025-04-13/  
[4] Christian immigrants helped elect Trump, now some are at risk of being deported, https://www.npr.org/2025/04/11/nx-s1-5345876/christian-immigrants-helped-elect-trump-now-some-are-at-risk-of-being-deported  

### 2.2 The Abrego García Case and Legal Challenges
The case of Kilmar Abrego García, a Maryland resident wrongly deported to El Salvador, has become a focal point of immigration disputes. El Salvador's President has stated he won't return García [1], while the Washington Post's editorial board has called for his return [2]. The administration's claim that it cannot return García is reportedly false [3], and there are calls for DHS and State Department officials to provide testimony [4]. Meanwhile, a judge has ordered the administration not to remove Venezuelans after the ACLU argued they were being "persecuted" as criminals [5].

[1] Salvadoran President Says He Won't Return Wrongly Deported Man, https://www.nytimes.com/video/world/americas/100000010110367/bukele-trump-deported-man.html  
[2] Washington Post Editorial Board- 'Return Abrego García to Maryland', https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2025/04/14/trump-bukele-elsalvador-deportation-maryland/  
[3] The Trump administration says it can't return Kilmar Abrego Garcia. That's false., https://www.msnbc.com/opinion/msnbc-opinion/trump-administration-says-cant-return-kilmar-abrego-garcia-s-false-rcna201198?cid=sm_npd_ms_wa_ma  
[4] It's time to compel officials at DHS and State to testify on Abrego García, https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2025/04/14/garcia-xinis-deportation-salvador-ms13/

### 2.3 ICE Operations and Enforcement
Immigration and Customs Enforcement operations have expanded in scope and location. The U.S. Army is now controlling land along the Mexico border where migrants could be detained [1]. ICE has detained Mohsen Mahdawi, a Palestinian green card holder and Columbia University student, during his citizenship interview [2], and additional Columbia students allegedly for pro-Palestinian activism [3]. In another case, the Department of Homeland Security incorrectly told a U.S. citizen who works as an immigration attorney to leave the country [4].

[1] US Army to control land on Mexico border as part of Base, migrants could be detained, officials say, https://apnews.com/article/border-trump-roosevelt-military-immigration-85974188a51593351eed70ad26291888

## 3. Foreign Policy and International Relations

### 3.1 Russia-Ukraine Conflict
Following a missile strike on Sumy that killed 35 people, Trump characterized it as a "mistake" [1], while European foreign ministers suggested "Putin is mocking Trump" and called for new sanctions [2]. Russia has reportedly targeted Sumy again [3]. Ukrainian President Zelensky has urged Trump to visit Ukraine before finalizing any deal with Russia [4]. The conflict has energy security implications for Europe, with EU nations facing a "dilemma" about potentially returning to Russian gas imports under Trump's foreign policy [5].

### 3.2 International Partnerships
Signs of strain in international relations are evident. European officials have reportedly been issued burner phones before traveling to the United States [1], suggesting significant security concerns. Germany's foreign policy is being shaped by considerations about both Trump and Putin [2], while Canada has pledged to increase defense spending to more than 2% of GDP [3]. U.S.-China relations appear strained, with analyses challenging Trump's assessment that he has China "on the ropes" [4].

## 4. Economic and Trade Policy

### 4.1 Tariffs Implementation and Challenges
The Trump administration's tariff policies face significant legal challenges, with lawsuits filed in the U.S. Court of International Trade [1]. Business groups argue that trade deficits do not constitute an emergency justifying these measures [2]. Reports indicate Trump is considering pausing auto tariffs amid global economic turbulence described as "whiplash" [3]. The administration's broader trade strategy is characterized as a "mess" by diplomatic sources [4].

### 4.2 Economic Indicators and Industry Impacts
Economic indicators suggest growing market concerns, with consumer confidence reportedly "cratering" amid recession fears [1]. An investor who predicted the 2008 collapse has issued a "stark new warning" described as "worse than a recession" [2]. Policy uncertainty is affecting specific sectors, with biotech experiencing a "deeper slump" due to unclear health policies [3]. GM CEO Mary Barra must navigate a $35 billion electric vehicle investment strategy in "Trump's America" [4].

### 4.3 Federal Budget and Spending Cuts
The Trump administration has proposed substantial spending cuts across multiple areas. A $9 billion spending reduction would target NPR, PBS, and foreign aid [1], while a separate plan would slash State Department funding by nearly half and reportedly end all funding for NATO and the UN [2]. Critics argue that these cuts, combined with tariff policies, appear designed to "move America down the value chain" by reducing scientific research funding [3].

Progressive leaders Bernie Sanders and Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez are conducting a "Fighting Oligarchy tour" that has drawn large crowds even in traditionally Republican states like Utah [1], with The Atlantic publishing an analysis of their approach [2]. ### 5.2 Political Violence and Threats
The Justice Department has charged a man with arson attacks on both a Tesla showroom and Republican headquarters in New Mexico [1]. In a separate case, a man accused of setting fire to Pennsylvania Governor Josh Shapiro's home allegedly stated he would have beaten the governor with a hammer [2] and now faces attempted murder and terrorism charges. The suspect reportedly confessed to "harboring hatred" and specifically targeting the Democratic governor [3].

## 6. Media and Public Opinion

### 6.1 Media Control and Public Opinion
Tensions between the administration and media organizations are evident, with Trump reportedly urging the Federal Communications Commission to punish '60 Minutes' over its reports on Greenland and Ukraine [1]. This suggestion has sparked internal FCC conflict, with Commissioner Gomez criticizing fellow Commissioner Brendan Carr for allegedly "abusing FCC authority to 'censor and control' journalists" [2]. Polling data reveals mixed political trends: a growing number of Republicans now identify with the MAGA movement [3], but voters are reportedly "not happy with Trump's trade war" [4] and no longer blaming Biden for current economic conditions [5].
